    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_410264897" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/410264897" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1489224-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338449051p2/1489224.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/410264897?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/1489224-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1489224-lisa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1489224-lisa?shelf=debbie-downer">debbie-downer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1489224-lisa?shelf=paranormal-romance-urban-fantasy">paranormal-romance-urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer410264897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10948874246340629460">I don't know if I've felt ever felt guiltier about not liking a book than I do about this one. So many people love <i>Unspoken</i> to pieces and I can understand why, but I was very underwhelmed. It seems to me that <i>Unspoken</i> was a book that was trying to break out of the YA mold but ended up following the fold. <br/><br/>By far the biggest problem with this novel is Jared Lynburn. He's your typical brooding, overprotective, woe-is-me, bad boy with anger management issues. I find none of these traits attractive, </span>
  <span id="freeText10948874246340629460" style="display:none">I don't know if I've felt ever felt guiltier about not liking a book than I do about this one. So many people love <i>Unspoken</i> to pieces and I can understand why, but I was very underwhelmed. It seems to me that <i>Unspoken</i> was a book that was trying to break out of the YA mold but ended up following the fold. <br /><br />By far the biggest problem with this novel is Jared Lynburn. He's your typical brooding, overprotective, woe-is-me, bad boy with anger management issues. I find none of these traits attractive, and therefore I could not identify with Kami's attraction to him even considering their shared thoughts. Although he and Kami are not in a relationship, he acts possessive of her. He has to be tricked into "letting" her go out with her girl friends without him, he sabotages her date with another guy, and he's always hovering around her in this creepy overprotective way, even when she tells him she needs space. <br /><br />I also found his self-pity very irritating and overly melodramatic, and I didn't appreciate how he would use his self-pity manipulatively to make Kami forgive him for his asinine behavior. He also had a tendency of expressing himself with physical violence. We're introduced to the character just after he gets into a fight with every member of the rugby team (we're given no explanation for this fight but I'm inclined to believe it was Jared's fault based on his subsequent actions), and he punches his cousin, Ash, in the face without any provocation. Physical assault is just not okay. <br /><br />When I was first introduced Kami Glass, I was intrigued. She was intelligent and witty, and I admired her ambition and strength. Kami also says the right things about not wanting a possessive boyfriend and needing independence, but in the end actions speak louder than words. While Kami initially admonishes Jared for his behavior, she quickly backs down and forgives him because he acts hurt by her criticism. I can't think of a single instance where she didn't end up comforting him and assuring him of his worth after he acted possessive, jealous, or overprotective. And even though his behaviors never change (he's possessive, overprotective, and jealous to the very end), she falls head over heels in love with him. By the end, I lost all respect I had for her character. <br /><br />I didn't find the side characters all that compelling either. There isn't much to say about Ash. He lacks personality and character development. He is the nice guy of the love triangle and he follows the path taken by nearly all other nice guys <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[he turns out to be evil, of course <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Angela's people-hate tip-toed the line between funny and annoying. Holly had potential in that she broke the YA mold by being pretty and popular with guys, yet also nice, however, she didn't have much depth. Kami's family was a bit too cartoonish for me, particularly her father, who joked the entire book. He doesn't have one line that wasn't supposed to be funny. <br /><br />Speaking of humor, I thought it was overdone. Not only was every character witty, which was very unrealistic, the characters would also make jokes during situations that called for serious reflection. The overuse of humor also made Kami and Jared's angst-filled relationship seem even more overly melodramatic because the scenes and conversations exploring their relationship were the only serious scenes in the entire book. <br /><br />As for the mystery, it was unnecessarily drawn out by lack of communication and characters inexplicably deciding not to follow up on information. Everyone in town seems to know the Lynburn secrets except Kami, Angela, Holly and Jared, despite the fact that Kami and Holly grew up in the town and are not outsiders, and Jared is a Lynburn. It seemed unrealistic that no one, including Kami's mother, would tell Kami what they knew about the Lynburns. There were also several instances where Jared's family would act strangely around him or say something cryptic, but instead of asking questions, he would just leave even though he supposedly wanted answers. His family wasn't even trying to hide the truth from him, and when he finally did ask for an explanation, they told him without a fight. <br /><br />Lastly, I thought the ending was problematic. Cliffhangers are one thing, but there still should be some sense of closure at the end of a book, despite unfinished plot lines. <i>Unspoken</i> felt like it was ended in the middle of the story, as though Brennan wrote the entire trilogy as one book and then randomly chopped into thirds. I wish the ending had been less abrupt <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and I also wish the Jared/Kami angst had been left out <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />The book gets an extra star for effort, but honestly, I didn't enjoy reading this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10948874246340629460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14350122156259046436">In Sorry-in-the-Vale, England, Kami has an Issue--she is a teenager who still talks with her invisible friend. Then the town's "ruling family" returns to the area, complete with teenaged cousins. Kami finds herself attracted to handsome Ash, but her world rocks when she meets brooding, reclusive cousin Jared.   <span id="freeText14350122156259046436" style="display:none">In Sorry-in-the-Vale, England, Kami has an Issue--she is a teenager who still talks with her invisible friend. Then the town's "ruling family" returns to the area, complete with teenaged cousins. Kami finds herself attracted to handsome Ash, but her world rocks when she meets brooding, reclusive cousin Jared. He is her invisible friend, and he is just as rattled to learn his own invisible friend is all too real. Interfering adults and a series of murders add notes of contemporary fiction and suspense fiction as well. It's a wild ride in a truly unique setting that's all Brennan's own. Don't miss it! </span>

<div id="review_355173254" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/355173254" />
    <a title="Kristalia " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia"><img alt="Kristalia " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535637983p2/5705623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/355173254?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristalia " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristalia " href="/user/show/5705623-kristalia">Kristalia </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=age-young-adult">age-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorite-couple">favorite-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=made-me-smile-or-laugh">made-me-smile-or-laugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=be-my-heroes-please">be-my-heroes-please</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=me-likey-mucho">me-likey-mucho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=wishlist_series">wishlist_series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer355173254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6027105770498179934"><b>Final rating: 4.75/5 stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381860i/739309._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='150' alt='unspoken' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was so sooooooooo good. I loved every part of it. Since i couldn't decide between 4 and 5 i decided it was going to be between. And it is only because i am type that craves for explanations and i didn't find enough of them in this book. For now, it is staying 5 stars as basic rating, because i feel it didn't belong with standard books.<br/><br/>I wanted to read it because it was written by Brennan. I loved her Demon's lexicon trilogy, and guess what, i love Unspoken even mor</span>
  <span id="freeText6027105770498179934" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 4.75/5 stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381860i/739309._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="150" alt="unspoken" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was so sooooooooo good. I loved every part of it. Since i couldn't decide between 4 and 5 i decided it was going to be between. And it is only because i am type that craves for explanations and i didn't find enough of them in this book. For now, it is staying 5 stars as basic rating, because i feel it didn't belong with standard books.<br><br>I wanted to read it because it was written by Brennan. I loved her Demon's lexicon trilogy, and guess what, i love Unspoken even more! I love her sense of humor and her writing style! The book made me laugh so many times, i almost fell from the chair once. Also, it was deeply emotional, especially when looking from Jared's POV.<br><br>There was never part that bore me, and i liked that. I loved that it was from alternating pov and in third person. It always makes story more believable to me (i don't like being in people's heads, aka, first person point, or narration).<br> <br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> Forest deep, silent bells<br>There’s a secret no one tells<br>Valley quiet, water still<br>Lynburns watching on the hill<br>Apples red, corn gold<br>Almost everyone grows old.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I found that a little creepy. So we have mysterious family, who were once rulers of the city. Now they are coming back after many many years. <br>I was wondering what was wrong with the family. I even thought they might be vampires. Guess what, they aren't. Mwahahaha. They wouldn't walk on the sun if they were and they certainly didn't sparkle.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>CHARACTERS</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br><br><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Kami</u>
  </i>
</b>: was soooooo cool. I loved her. And she was interesting and funny. She shares mental connection with Jared, her imaginary friend, who guess what, goes in package with Lynburns. She thought she made him up, until she went into the elevator with him. That is when they both understood that they were in fact real people. I love her courage, and the fact that she was willing to investigate Lynburns and the town in general, even breaking into the offices and taking documents. Wow. She even has friends who will help her, and she is not miss popular type everybody must love me. She is just normal with voice in her head.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“If I wasn't going to be a world-famous journalist and if I didn't have such respect for truth and justice, I could be an amazing master criminal.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I especially loved the part where she fell in the well, and Jared went to rescue her(I laughed soooo soooooooooo much):<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “Honestly, Jared, one thing at a time. Why are you in the well with me? This is a really bad rescue!”<br>“You lost consciousness and slipped under the surface of the water!” Jared pointed out. “There was no time.”<br>“But now we’re both trapped! Now we’re both going to die!”<br>“No, we’re not,” said Jared. “I called the police as I was running to the well. I’m sure they’re coming.”<br>“Did they say they were coming?” Kami asked suspiciously. “Or did you shout ‘Kami’s in the well!’ and then jump in the well too, thus losing your phone and making sure that the police think it was some kids playing a dumb joke?”<br>Jared paused. He was breathing quickly, the dreamy part of Kami noticed, his chest rising and falling hard. She wasn’t sure if it was because he’d had to run so fast, because he’d had to dive to grab her, or if it was panic.<br>“Alternate plan,” Jared said. “Do you have a very intelligent collie who might communicate through a system of barks to your parents that little Kami is in the well?”<br>Kami closed her eyes and leaned her cheek against the wet planes of Jared’s collarbone.<br>“We’re going to die.” Something else dawned on her. “And where is your shirt?”<br>“Let me explain,” said Jared. “I had just gone to bed, like a reasonable person, when you decided to get tossed into a well like a crazy person. And then it was a matter of some urgency to reach you. You’re lucky I tripped over my jeans on the way out the door.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Jared</u>
  </i>
</b>: I loved him. I understand him too. His father is dead, and his mother is the one who even blamed the fault on him. He was in fact, an outcast of the family, because his mother was never meant to marry his father. He is so so devastated that he has no one, while he has family. His sadness and closing to the world are especially shown in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16002855.The_Spring_Before_I_Met_You__The_Lynburn_Legacy___0_25_" title="The Spring Before I Met You (The Lynburn Legacy, #0.25) by Sarah Rees Brennan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spring Before I Met You</a>, where the only person who would talk to him was his imaginary friend Kami. Who was real person. Since he didn't have proper relationship with people, he often confused his feelings with something they are not. There was scene when his family went to dance in the rain, and he started to lose it, while Kami tried to give him support; I loved how she was always there for him, always taking his side. <br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Listen to me. I don’t know what’s going on. I don’t know what any of this means. But I know this much. It doesn’t matter. You’re not one of them. You never were. You’re not theirs. You’re mine.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>OVERALL</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br><br>I loved the story in general. There were always funny moments, and always emotional ones. I loved the mystery, the killings and the Lynburns. It was interesting that the most of the things was explained in so-so logical way. I loved loved loved especially the scene with the wall between them. I loved that moment, and i think it was one of the best in the book. <br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>There was a wall between them, but the wall of silence in Jared’s head wasn’t there anymore. Kami still did not quite dare to come to the place where their minds met, for fear of being shut out again. She skirted the edge of what he was feeling, and stretched out her hand so he could see it on his side of the stone wall.<br>After a moment, she felt the brush of Jared’s fingers against hers. The light touch of skin on skin made electricity crackle through her blood so that it burned and stung in her veins.<br>She had never been so aware of anyone in her life, or so uncomfortable.<br>Jared’s hand closed around hers, their fingers linking. From a careful touch of fingertips,they were suddenly both clinging as if the other had fallen off a cliff and they had to keep hold or risk them slipping away. Jared’s hand was a lot bigger than Kami’s, fingers callused.<br>It was just a boy’s hand, blood and flesh and bone, she told herself fiercely. It wasn’t such a big deal.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>
  <i>This review can be found on my blog: <a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">infinity-of-time.blogspot.com</a> also known as... </i>
</b><br><a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/2013/04/unspoken-lynburn-legacy-1-by-sarah-rees.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363317i/714576.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer296349231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11214401721333838429">This is the book for all of you who still have a little piece of a child left in your soul. Characters are seventeen, but maybe you'll have impression that they are younger than that. That's for the most part because of the writing style - it has <i>fairytaleish</i> vibe combined with mystery. <br/><br/>Kami Glass - yes, I liked her from the first page when I saw her name - is a strong girl, a little bit strange but in a good way, and she knows what she wants. If you're expecting some usual YA love story with pa</span>
  <span id="freeText11214401721333838429" style="display:none">This is the book for all of you who still have a little piece of a child left in your soul. Characters are seventeen, but maybe you'll have impression that they are younger than that. That's for the most part because of the writing style - it has <i>fairytaleish</i> vibe combined with mystery. <br /><br />Kami Glass - yes, I liked her from the first page when I saw her name - is a strong girl, a little bit strange but in a good way, and she knows what she wants. If you're expecting some usual YA love story with paranormal twist, think again. <i>Unspoken</i> is completely different from any book you've read. <br /><br />But ending... My God, ending! It's killing me. True cliffhanger. I wanted to smash my Kindle out of spite to the goddess of writen word - how dare she to torture me this way? </span>
  <a data-text-id="11214401721333838429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/955689287?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Regan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Regan" href="/user/show/19645927-regan">Regan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375871030" href="/book/show/17162405-unspoken">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19645927-regan?shelf=books-owned-read">books-owned-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer955689287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14952035705160892026">4.5 SO ADDICTING! And the main character is hilarious </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_336229185" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/336229185" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/336229185?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=netgalley-e-book">netgalley-e-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer336229185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2383496220428745615">Unspoken is not the story I was expecting, and I enjoyed that. Somehow I thought this would be a dark and serious tale, and some of it is. Mostly, it was a story full of wit and fun, a little romance, and magic. <br/><br/>Unspoken is centered on Kami Glass, a high-school student, and ambitious journalist-in-training. She’s head of the school newspaper, and always on the trail of a new story. But now Kami’s focused on uncovering secrets, because the founding family of Sorry-in-the-Vale, The Lynburn’s, have</span>
  <span id="freeText2383496220428745615" style="display:none">Unspoken is not the story I was expecting, and I enjoyed that. Somehow I thought this would be a dark and serious tale, and some of it is. Mostly, it was a story full of wit and fun, a little romance, and magic. <br /><br />Unspoken is centered on Kami Glass, a high-school student, and ambitious journalist-in-training. She’s head of the school newspaper, and always on the trail of a new story. But now Kami’s focused on uncovering secrets, because the founding family of Sorry-in-the-Vale, The Lynburn’s, have come back, after a seventeen year absence, and no one thinks this is a good thing. There’s one more thing you need to know about Kami: she’s grown up with an imaginary friend (or so she thinks), Jared. When the Lynburn boys show up in school, Kami finds out that Jared is not an imaginary friend at all, but a real live flesh and blood boy. A boy not happy to find out that <i>his</i> imaginary friend is anything but. Kami is shocked, as well, but this has to take a backseat to the strange occurrences that start happening around her. <br /><br />Animal sacrifices, an attempt on her life, and the murder of a girl, become the mysteries that must be solved. Is it a coincidence that all this has happened since the Lynburn’s return? Kami doesn’t think so. Everywhere she turns she gets a warning to stay away from the Lynburn’s, they’re dangerous, but why? Even her mother begs her to stay away from Jared, but Kami knows she can’t. To stay away from him would be like tearing herself in half. <br /><br />Kami is such a quirky, unstoppable, and fun force. Her sense of humor was dry, witty and sharp. It was impossible not to be enamored with her from the get-go. Kami’s always thought of herself as a bit crazy, knowing normal people didn’t have an imaginary friend. When she finds out Jared is real, she knows that some sort of magic must exist and be involved. Kami can’t help but be tentative and frightened of Jared, because he knows so many of her inner thoughts and secrets. Someone like that can hold so much power over you. <br /><br />Jared is angry to find out Kami is real too, for the same reasons. He’s a moody, broody, male and doesn’t like that he’s so vulnerable to Kami. But soon they sort out most of their anger, and become closer than ever before. Jared is fiercely protective of Kami now that he knows someone’s out to kill her. He can’t lose Kami, the most important connection in his life; someone who’s always been in his corner, even when his family has not. I found myself rooting for their brewing romance even as they fought so hard against it. I wanted to scream: “Kiss her, dammit!” These two go back and forth and had me laughing some of the time. Here’s a fun quote:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“A leather jacket,” Kami said as he shrugged into it. “Aren’t you trying a little too hard to play into certain bad boy clichés?” <br />“Nah,” said Jared. “You’re thinking of black leather. Black leather’s for bad boys. It’s all in the color. You wouldn’t think I was a bad boy if I was wearing a pink leather jacket.” <br />“That’s true,” Kami said. “What I would think of you, I do not know. So what does brown leather mean, then?”<br />“I’m going for manly,” Jared said. “Maybe a little rugged.”<br />“It’s bits of a dead cow, don’t ask it to perform miracles.”-Kami</i>
</b><br /><br />There are a few twists and turns that keep you guessing who’s at the bottom of this mystery. Suspicion is cast on everyone. There’s a fun cast of secondary characters, as well: Angela, Kami’s perpetually annoyed and unfailingly loyal best friend. Rusty, Angela’s brother, a self-defense instructor always leaping out on the two of them to keep their defenses sharp. Holly, the eager new friend. Kami’s father and little brothers, Ten, who is ten, and seven year-old, Tomo, also bring a lot of random and silly humor to the story. The Lynburn family figures in prominently, but they are far from fun. <br /><br />I had two complaints with the story, one bigger than the other. First, the writing felt a little disjointed and choppy in places. Not a smooth transition from one happening to the next. Not a huge issue but it took some getting used to. My second complaint is a much bigger deal to me: the HORRIBLE cliffhanger we’re left on!! Why, why, why?!! Ugh!! I have no patience whatsoever, and now I’m forced to wait until next June to find out what happens! In spite of these complaints, I did really enjoy the story and I’m eagerly anticipating the sequel. <br /><br /><i>Thanks to Random House Books for Young Readers and Netgalley for allowing me to read this.</i> <br /><br />You can find this review and more at <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2012/09/review-unspoken-by-sarah-rees-brennan.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den.</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2383496220428745615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Carrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie"><img alt="Carrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415677371p2/36817401.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1747928559?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie">Carrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13574672-unspoken">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1747928559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16629147293631164317">Kami Glass has always talked to a boy in her head ever since she was born. She's always thought of him as an imaginary friend and loved him all of her life keeping the voice a secret so others will not see her as crazy. But when the mysterious Lynburn family return one of the teenage boys seems very familiar to Kami. <br/><br/>Kami soon finds that her best friend that she's always had in her head is really Jared Lynburn. When an attempt is made on Kami's life Jared quickly proves that he does know all of </span>
  <span id="freeText16629147293631164317" style="display:none">Kami Glass has always talked to a boy in her head ever since she was born. She's always thought of him as an imaginary friend and loved him all of her life keeping the voice a secret so others will not see her as crazy. But when the mysterious Lynburn family return one of the teenage boys seems very familiar to Kami. <br /><br />Kami soon finds that her best friend that she's always had in her head is really Jared Lynburn. When an attempt is made on Kami's life Jared quickly proves that he does know all of Kami's thoughts. Now Kami is determined to discover who was behind the attempt and how and why she seem to be connected to the mysterious Jared Lynburn.<br /><br />Unspoken by Sarah Rees Brennan is the first book in the Lynburn Legacy series. I would first and foremost warn to readers that this is one of those that leave you on a bit of a cliffhanger that will continue in the rest of the series. <br /><br />For this first book I enjoyed some of the ideas involved in it but unfortunately for me it was just way too slow paced read to keep my attention all throughout. When I get to over halfway in a story and am still waiting out answers to questions brought up in the opening pages I get extremely frustrated and I believe it was over 60% before some questions were getting addressed. Even at the end I just wanted to hurry the action along. <br /><br />Overall, 2.5 stars. Too slow paced for my taste but some interesting content nonetheless. <br /><br />For more reviews please visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://carriesbookreviews.wordpress.com/">https://carriesbookreviews.wordpress....</a><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13695329919624931627">i picked this book up cause the concept was too interesting & different.<br/>Kami can hear a voice in her her head & talk to someonelse all her life in her mind. & the author did not disappoint. the story kept me every bit curious as it could. like is this person for real or imaginary. if real so how was it possible? <br/>Jared's character is way too complicated & troubled. the solidity to rely on, for him has always been kami, as she is the comforting & supporting voice in his head. also i did not like h</span>
  <span id="freeText13695329919624931627" style="display:none">i picked this book up cause the concept was too interesting &amp; different.<br />Kami can hear a voice in her her head &amp; talk to someonelse all her life in her mind. &amp; the author did not disappoint. the story kept me every bit curious as it could. like is this person for real or imaginary. if real so how was it possible? <br />Jared's character is way too complicated &amp; troubled. the solidity to rely on, for him has always been kami, as she is the comforting &amp; supporting voice in his head. also i did not like how everyone was always harsh on him. no-one seem care about him except for the voice in his head. he did not deserve such family. even throughout the book the Lyburns did not seem to really accept or care for him. always kept secrets &amp; kept him in the dark. everywhere he was just treated &amp; assumed as villain. partly because he was not as good looking as his cousin?<br />also Kami's character was a joy to read. ambitious, strong, funny, self- sufficient.<br /> The struggle between Kami &amp; Jared, from being voice in head to real people is captured beautifully. the emotional &amp; physical. the mystery regarding the Lyburns did keep me guessing to as in what type of supernatural Lyburn's were. <br />this book balances everything. love, friendship, family, hate, paranormal, which is rare in ya.</span>

<div id="review_302053162" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/302053162" />
    <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine"><img alt="Mimi Valentine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1314137947p2/6110599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/302053162?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi Valentine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi Valentine" href="/user/show/6110599-mimi-valentine">Mimi Valentine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=best-of-2012">best-of-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=boys-i-wish-were-real">boys-i-wish-were-real</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=pure-awesomeness">pure-awesomeness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6110599-mimi-valentine?shelf=adorable-favourites">adorable-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer302053162" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12327152247680538606">There's "bizarre" and "different," and then there's this book... which is probably the best of both! I loooooooooooooooooooooved it so much! <br/><br/><b>Unspoken</b> is one of those books that make you slap your forehead and wonder why you hadn't read it earlier. I couldn't stop grinning, yet at the same time, I couldn't breathe when it got intense. It kind of has the feel to it of <b>Beautiful Creatures</b> — small town, fantastic cast, feared magical family, and rich gothic mystery — except I liked this much, much m</span>
  <span id="freeText12327152247680538606" style="display:none">There's "bizarre" and "different," and then there's this book... which is probably the best of both! I loooooooooooooooooooooved it so much! <br /><br /><b>Unspoken</b> is one of those books that make you slap your forehead and wonder why you hadn't read it earlier. I couldn't stop grinning, yet at the same time, I couldn't breathe when it got intense. It kind of has the feel to it of <b>Beautiful Creatures</b> — small town, fantastic cast, feared magical family, and rich gothic mystery — except I liked this much, much more! <br /><br />Kami and Jared make up a totally unorthodox pair that I seriously LOVE! ♥ They've never met before (they used to believe that the other was imaginary), but they've been able to talk into each other's minds since birth. People look at them strangely for stopping randomly to laugh at inner conversations, but Kami and Jared don't care. They've been best friends since forever, and they're like two halves of the same whole. <br /><br />And when they <i>do</i> finally meet, it's so realistic! They don't know what to be at first (Friends? Girlfriend/boyfriend? Enemies?), but I promise your heart will go for a wild ride. <br /><br />It's not just the romance that's so different from what I'm used to, but the characters themselves. Kami (witty teenage journalist extraordinaire) is strange and she knows it. But there's no angsty outcast drama here! She still has wonderful friends and a wonderful family despite her strangeness. And Jared... Jared is a leather-jacket-wearing bad boy who'd move heaven and Earth for Kami. My heart broke for him, ached for him, shone for him.<br /><br />The wit is off the charts! Kami has such a smart mouth and the kind of reckless brain all reporters are born with; the banter had me cracking up constantly. Sarah Rees Brennan is a mastermind at creating a dynamic story filled with wonderfully unique characters, NONE of that hair-pulling cliche drama, and ALL of the intenseness of a great mystery. <br /><br />Brilliantly witty and fantastically strange, <b>Unspoken</b> is an amazing novel that brings everything we've been looking for in YA without even knowing it! With a hilarious cast, smile-inducing dialogue, and a mystery that turns pages on its own, this book is sure to be a stunner! :) <br /><br /><b>BUY or BORROW?:</b> This book was buy-worthy the moment Kami cracked her first joke! I want to own this for all of its hilarious one-liners and originality, and you should too! ;)<br /><br />(Original review at <a href="http://diminutivemimi.blogspot.ca/2012/07/review-unspoken.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Mimi Valentine's YA Review Blog</a>) </span>
  <a data-text-id="12327152247680538606" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1087946370" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1087946370" />
    <a title="Cody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35007929-cody"><img alt="Cody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415626292p2/35007929.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1087946370?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody" href="/user/show/35007929-cody">Cody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1087946370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4735976499750584105"><b>Shows great great promise!</b><br/><br/>This is my first book by Brennan and I was pleasantly surprised as it is truly like no other. Just look at that blurb: the ability to talk to someone in your head and then a bad boy in leather turns up on a motorcycle? <i>*Fangirls*</i> No longer an imaginary friend but a hot guy? Are her feelings real? What does she want? WHO does she want? Filled with angst and a tantalizing slow burn romance? YES YES YES YES Y’HES!<br/><br/>Kami Glass is an ambitious wanna be journalist who is always</span>
  <span id="freeText4735976499750584105" style="display:none"><b>Shows great great promise!</b><br /><br />This is my first book by Brennan and I was pleasantly surprised as it is truly like no other. Just look at that blurb: the ability to talk to someone in your head and then a bad boy in leather turns up on a motorcycle? <i>*Fangirls*</i> No longer an imaginary friend but a hot guy? Are her feelings real? What does she want? WHO does she want? Filled with angst and a tantalizing slow burn romance? YES YES YES YES Y’HES!<br /><br />Kami Glass is an ambitious wanna be journalist who is always looking for scandal and wanting to uncover the towns darkest secrets. Kami made this book for me; she’s intelligent, entertaining and funny. I loved her attitude towards her family and boys as she believes that being independent is important and to never be possessed by anyone or let them put you down. She’s one of the most determined and ambitious heroines I’ve ever met and she has gone through the typical woes of childhood with school friends finding her weird but she refuses to let people’s opinions interfere with her aspirations.<br /><br />When Kami is attacked with no clear suspect and animal sacrifices keep occurring throughout the town Kami is determined to discover the truth. As previously said Kami has had an imaginary friend Jared since she was born. Then Jared comes crashing into town and Kami realises; one shes not crazy and two the person who knows every little detail about her is real.<br /><br />The lengths the author goes to in order to make the connection between Kami and Jared real is absolutely amazing both mentally and physically. It’s so realistic with no insta-love because obviously you’d be in complete horror if this happened to you! The romance is different from other YA books which is both good and bad because I seriously didn’t know what was going to happen but the tension is delicious, you will not suddenly turn the page and find kisses and declarations of love I hate to spoil this but you hardly get anything from the first book! <s>YES I’m already reading the second, Ooops.</s> Jared = Hot, Broody, has a Deathwish, Bad Temper, Scars.. that it all ;)<br /><br />So why not 5 stars? It took me a while to actually enjoy reading this book, slow starter however it quickly picked up towards the end and the cliffhanger which was just cruel will have you wanting more!<br /><br /><b>NOTE:</b> Yes this may be 3 stars but I’m already half way through Untold and it is without a doubt 10 times better. You need this epic series! <i>WHERE HAVE YOU BEEN ALL MY LIFE?</i><br /><br /><a href="http://literary-lyobsessed.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Literary-ly Obsessed</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4735976499750584105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2623420398" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2623420398" />
    <a title="Jennie Damron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74229376-jennie-damron"><img alt="Jennie Damron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604192048p2/74229376.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2623420398?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennie Damron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennie Damron" href="/user/show/74229376-jennie-damron">Jennie Damron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2623420398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1857625949349772908">I love Gothic books. Hands down my favorite type of book to read. This book was a great Gothic read. The atmosphere, spooky house, and creepy woods were all on point. At times Kami got on my nerves. Her trying to joke or lighten a moment would be a mood breaker and disrupt the flow of the story. Set that aside, the book was great. The plot moved well and the characters likable. I will definitely be reading the next on the series. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_488916348" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/488916348" />
    <a title="S.J. Kincaid" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4874022-s-j-kincaid"><img alt="S.J. Kincaid" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498176746p2/4874022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/488916348?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S.J. Kincaid" class="user" itemprop="url" name="S.J. Kincaid" href="/user/show/4874022-s-j-kincaid">S.J. Kincaid</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer488916348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer423770299499119307">What a fun, cute book. Although I think the magical world still needs some fleshing out (I trust that will happen in book two), I really loved the characters, and even the Kami/Jared relationship. It's very rare for me to appreciate romance in most YAs, so it's all the better to discover a great one here between two well-developed characters. I look forward to the next one.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_415473712" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/415473712" />
    <a title="Buka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2785399-buka"><img alt="Buka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1270298390p2/2785399.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/415473712?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Buka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Buka" href="/user/show/2785399-buka">Buka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2785399-buka?shelf=thanks-but-no-thanks">thanks-but-no-thanks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2785399-buka?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer415473712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer89068415739331877">My relationship with Sarah Rees Brennan's books is like a see-saw. I liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6479419-the-demon-s-lexicon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Demon's Lexicon</a> but was annoyed by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6594657-the-demon-s-covenant' rel='nofollow noopener'>Demon's Covenant</a>, I really liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12640578-team-human' rel='nofollow noopener'>Team Human</a> (written with Justine Larbaleister) and - once again - was really annoyed by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10866624-unspoken' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unspoken</a>. This is Sara Rees Brennan of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6594657-the-demon-s-covenant' rel='nofollow noopener'>Demon's Covenant</a> and everything irritating that I remember about it is here again. <br/>It's one more book where everything - characters, pacing, plot, mood - can and will be sacrificed in order to deliver at least one more witty one-l</span>
  <span id="freeText89068415739331877" style="display:none">My relationship with Sarah Rees Brennan's books is like a see-saw. I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6479419-the-demon-s-lexicon" rel="nofollow noopener">Demon's Lexicon</a> but was annoyed by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6594657-the-demon-s-covenant" rel="nofollow noopener">Demon's Covenant</a>, I really liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12640578-team-human" rel="nofollow noopener">Team Human</a> (written with Justine Larbaleister) and - once again - was really annoyed by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10866624-unspoken" rel="nofollow noopener">Unspoken</a>. This is Sara Rees Brennan of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6594657-the-demon-s-covenant" rel="nofollow noopener">Demon's Covenant</a> and everything irritating that I remember about it is here again. <br />It's one more book where everything - characters, pacing, plot, mood - can and will be sacrificed in order to deliver at least one more witty one-liner. And, unlike <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12640578-team-human" rel="nofollow noopener">Team Human</a> (which, I think, had even less jokes), this is not a satire. At least, nobody seems to think so. I checked.<br /><br />So here I am, staring at a page full of gushing 5 and 4-star reviews, wondering is there something wrong with me? I mean, I like humor. One of my very favourite fantasy authors (she's Russian, so I don't shelve her books here on Goodreads) writes mostly humorous novels. I love heroes who are not all about aaangst and serious bsns. But as for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10866624-unspoken" rel="nofollow noopener">Unspoken</a>, well... for instance, I don't think Kami's father had said a single sentence that didn't have a joke in it. <br />A mother leaves her daughter alone in bed with a boy for the whole night and doesn't even check on them - all so they can be caught in the morning by the father which results in a whole torrent of witticisms. Am I only one who sees problems with that whole scenario? Or, a more spoilery one: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a girl is killed. Horribly killed in a small sleepy English town. But who cares? Next morning we are back to playful banter. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />One more really annoying fact about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10866624-unspoken" rel="nofollow noopener">Unspoken</a> is how awfully convenient it was when author needed it. You know that mystery novels where everything is neatly solved because the criminal left a huge incriminating piece of evidence right at the crime scene? Unspoken is one of these stories. Our supposedly hyperactive and nosy main girl - the self-appointed investigator - not pursuing a couple of leads that were dangled in front of her for days? I just can't buy it. Or <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[how long did it take for Jared to reach Kami when she was pushed in the well? To me it felt like 10-20 seconds at max. So where was his speed when they stumbled through the forest for what felt like an hour? Or what about telling a girl you don't want anywhere near you all about the tremendous power she has over your relative? Uh-huh. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I really wanted to like this book. I love "telepatically speaking to each other" idea. In fact, I wish, there were more about it in the book. But it seems, for every good thing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10866624-unspoken" rel="nofollow noopener">Unspoken</a> has going for it, there are a couple of bad or annoying ones. It's a page-turner that turns anticlimatic in the end. It's all about girl power and her deciding for herself. Yep, and rather than shown, it's shouted at you IN NO UNCERTAIN TERMS.<br />I told myself: look, self, it's so funny! So humorous, it's humorous even in serious moments, epic moments, creepy moments which often promptly felt pompous, small-scale or nothing special because, you know, funny can do that to a scene.<br />But, argued self, but it defies some tried to death genre conventions, like "mystical karmic connection = soulmates". And it also has a Love Triangle of Doom, a Tortured Hero and "oh no, there is no way he loves me, even though everything is pointing to it".<br /><br />I don't know if I'll read the sequel, although the cliff-hanger in the end will do it's damnedest to make sure you'll do. Right now I don't really want to but, judging by my luck with Sarah Rees Brennan's books, I'm bound to like the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="89068415739331877" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10442598420894639337">2nd Re-Read : October, 7th<br/>Still as good as the first time I read it! :)<br/>______________"_________________________<br/>This book has one of the most intriguing plots allied with a vast, vast number of quirky characters, that I've ever encountered in a story.<br/><br/>In fact, I've never encountered such a number of strange, a little out of this world, lovable characters! It was great!<br/><br/>There's <b>Kami</b>, our fearless reporter: <i>"Kami had been hearing a voice in her head all her life. When she was eight, people had though</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10442598420894639337" style="display:none">2nd Re-Read : October, 7th<br />Still as good as the first time I read it! :)<br />______________"_________________________<br />This book has one of the most intriguing plots allied with a vast, vast number of quirky characters, that I've ever encountered in a story.<br /><br />In fact, I've never encountered such a number of strange, a little out of this world, lovable characters! It was great!<br /><br />There's <b>Kami</b>, our fearless reporter: <i>"Kami had been hearing a voice in her head all her life. When she was eight, people had thought it was cute that she had an imaginary friend. It was very different now that she was seventeen. Kami was accustomed to people thinking she was crazy"</i><br /><br />Kami's best friend, <b>Angela</b>, who <u>really</u> likes to take naps <i>“Nap,” Angela finished, in the reverent tones of a knight who has finally spotted the Holy Grail</i> Then she may be considered as a little anti-social:<i>“What are these people doing here, Kami? You know I don’t like people.”</i><br /><br />Kami's dad, <b>Jon</b> who is just O.o :<i>“Stay away from him. Stay away from them all until you’re of marrying age. Once you reach a nice, mature fifty-four, gentlemen callers will be welcomed here.”</i> Great character! lol<br /><br />Kami's brothers:<br /><br />What Kami says about <b>Tomo</b>: <i>“The current theory is that he is a lemonade vampire."</i><br /><br />Then there's <b>Ten</b>( the poor kid is ten years old): <i>“I am considering becoming a vegetarian,” he announced in a low voice.<br />“Not that this isn’t excellent and nutritious,” he told Mum, blinking worriedly. “But I might owe it to my conscience.”</i><br /><br />Kami's friend, <b>Holly</b>: <i>“I used to have an imaginary friend when I was seven,” Holly contributed. “A unicorn called Princess Zelda.”</i><br /><br />Angela's brother, <b>Rusty</b>, who <u>really</u> likes the notion of free meals: <i>Rusty collapsed back on the hearthrug. “Have fun, and don’t be home late. I get dinner out of babysitting, right?”</i><br /><br />Then there's <b>Jared</b>: <i>“Hark,” he said, his tone very dry. “What stone through yonder window breaks?”<br />Kami yelled up at him, “It is the east, and Juliet is a jerk!”</i><br /><br />Kami has known Jared for most of her life. He has been literally a voice in her head, since always. So when these two finally see each other in the flesh, the shock is of epic proportions...<br /><br />Their reaction to one another felt too viscerally violent, at least to me it did...<br />They've known each other forever, and all of a sudden they can't even stand to touch one another (well, one of them..).<br /><br /><br />There was one thing I would have liked if it had been sorted out: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Who threw Kami down the well? Or was it a side effect of Jared's magic? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />And then there was the attack on <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Holly. One of the random sorcerers did it? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Or did I miss something?<br /><br />Also could have done without the attempted love triangle. Ash was just...(I'm twitching my nose, and making scary faces...)<br /><br />And then there was that <b>FINALE....WTH????</b> I was not a happy reader when I read that last page(and although I understand it, it doesn't mean that I have to like it, though!)<br /><br />And then there was <b>that</b> spoiler, that I read concerning the next book O.o ...you know what? I'm completely clueless, right now!<br />p.s. DON'T READ ANY SPOILERS THE AUTHOR GIVES YOU!!<br />BEWARE: THEY ARE POISONED....SPOILERS!!<br /></span>

<div id="review_951409703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/951409703" />
    <a title="Anna (Enchanted by YA)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya"><img alt="Anna (Enchanted by YA)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426518362p2/30983445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/951409703?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna (Enchanted by YA)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna (Enchanted by YA)" href="/user/show/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya">Anna (Enchanted by YA)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375871030" href="/book/show/17162405-unspoken">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=beautiful-writing">beautiful-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=great-characters">great-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=impossible-not-to-love">impossible-not-to-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=needed-more-pages">needed-more-pages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=super-ending">super-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=swoonworthy-love-interest">swoonworthy-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30983445-anna-enchanted-by-ya?shelf=twists-and-turns">twists-and-turns</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer951409703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15374532222712032428">For what I’d consider a “well-known book”, I’d heard surprisingly little going into Unspoken and with such a vague synopsis I was intrigued… After the first few pages I was hooked.<br/><br/>The mystery aspect was done so well in that we get enough information to keep the momentum going, but not enough to feel satisfied. There never failed to be something more to come which I loved. Most of this led up to (several) big reveals where the pace really picks up until it’s impossible to stop reading. That endin</span>
  <span id="freeText15374532222712032428" style="display:none">For what I’d consider a “well-known book”, I’d heard surprisingly little going into Unspoken and with such a vague synopsis I was intrigued… After the first few pages I was hooked.<br><br>The mystery aspect was done so well in that we get enough information to keep the momentum going, but not enough to feel satisfied. There never failed to be something more to come which I loved. Most of this led up to (several) big reveals where the pace really picks up until it’s impossible to stop reading. That ending though… Not okay!<br><br>Moving on before I abandon this review and either start screaming or looking for the second book (possibly both if I can’t get it straight away), let’s talk about the characters. I have to say Sarah Rees Brennan is exceptional at writing people who you instantly feel something towards (I don’t say love because with a certain bad boy *cough*Jared*cough* I was constantly going back and forth between wanting to punch and kiss him).<br><br>Every character is so unique with their own personality quirks and my favourite parts in the book were scenes with many together because the dynamics are brilliant, and often hilarious! The main protagonist Kami has great humour and is very relatable with a strive to get answers, be it for her school newspaper or herself, trying to figure out what the hell was going on in town and how she fits into it.<br><br>There’s no doubt in my mind that I’d recommend you pick up Unspoken. With its supernatural mystery, eclectic cast of characters and entertaining dialogue it was my perfect read – maybe it will be yours too!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446935765ra/16929468.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Posted on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://enchantedbyya.blogspot.co.uk">http://enchantedbyya.blogspot.co.uk</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15374532222712032428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ngvsi1kBY9YaUDk+6apHlyrVfSiaOmYgPktaDMh8UfoMLYVZ4l+qvr17jV8eX01I/Iqa4FS36EdlNRy9BT+jYA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aPvrTrxqAnEQpKK9LLJC7m+IC1rDMM0MmvcjWrCGJ+hS3YKcBzTLGbePFtzbR0gxudfskg29Q2vBiWXrfcXVcg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer53702209764815032">Sarah Rees Brennan is Irish and currently lives in Dublin. She's been writing YA books for more than ten years, which is terrifying to contemplate! She hopes you (yes you!) find at least one of them to be the kind of book you remember.</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/15781826-unspoken">Quotes from Unspoken</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Hark,” he said, his tone very dry. “What stone through yonder window breaks?”<br />Kami yelled up at him, “It is the east, and Juliet is a jerk!”<br />Jared abandoned Shakespeare and demanded, “What do you think you’re doing?”<br />“Throwing a pebble,” said Kami defensively. “Uh… and I’ll pay for the window.”<br />Jared vanished and Kami was ready to start shouting again, when he reemerged with the pebble clenched in his fist. “This isn’t a pebble! This is a <i>rock</i>.”<br />“It’s possible that your behaviour has inspired some negative feelings that caused me to pick a slightly overlarge pebble,” Kami admitted.&rdquo;</span>

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;What the hell is going on?" demanded Kami's dad, advancing with his black eyes snapping. Jared blurted, "My intentions are honourable."<br />Kami sat up straight in her bed and stared in Jared's direction. "Are you completely crazy?" she wanted to know. "This isn't the eighteenth century. How do you think that's going to help?"<br />"Well, I mean," Jared said, back against the wall like a cornered animal. "When we're older. I mean-"<br />"Please shut up," Kami begged.<br />"I agree with Kami," said Dad. "When you're in an abyss-like hole, quit digging.&rdquo;</span>
